# What is Aster? | Aster

[Aster](https://www.asterdex.com/en)
 ($ASTER) is a next-generation decentralized perpetual exchange built for everyone.

Following Astherus' merger with APX Finance in late 2024, this new identity is more than just a name change. We’re revolutionizing the way people trade perpetual contracts and utilize assets in the decentralized world.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/#why-aster)

Why Aster?

Aster is our unified vision to simplify and elevate the DeFi experience. It’s a platform where security, performance, and community-first design come together. Industry leaders recognized Astherus for its powerful yield-generating products and APX for its robust perpetual trading infrastructure. Now, with Aster, we combine those strengths to build a seamless ecosystem — one where traders and earners alike can access everything they need without friction. From one-click trading to smart automation and deep on-chain liquidity, Aster is rethinking how DeFi should work — simple, efficient, and built for users.

**Perps are a multi-billion-dollar market**: Multi-chain perpetual trading is Aster’s core product. Since 2024, perpetual decentralized exchanges have captured hundreds of billions in cumulative volume on a monthly basis ([DefiLlama](https://defillama.com/perps)
). With deep expertise, Aster now delivers a high-leverage, private, and dual-mode trading experience. We are uniquely positioned to capture a significant portion of this hundred-billion-dollar market opportunity.

**New identity, clear focus**: Aster is now laser-focused on building the best decentralized perpetual exchange in the space. We're committed to delivering a seamless, powerful, and truly decentralized on-chain derivatives trading experience.

[Stage 1: Spectra](https://docs.asterdex.com/stage-1-spectra/aster-spectra-stage-1)

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/#delve-into-aster)

Delve into Aster


---------------------------------------------------------------------

Aster introduces three seamless trading modes:

*   [**Perpetual Mode (Pro**](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/v1/BTCUSDT)
    **)**: Perpetuals trading using order book interface with deep liquidity, extremely low trading fees, and advanced trading tools
    
*   [**1001x**](mailto:undefined)
    : Perpetuals trading using on-chain liquidity, one-click, MEV-resistant perpetual contracts trading
    
*   [**Spot mode**](https://www.asterdex.com/en/spot/ASTERUSDT)
    **:** Spot trading using order book interface with deep liquidity, extremely low trading fees and advanced trading tools
    

We continue to support Astherus’ popular yield products under **Aster Earn**, including the BNB liquid staking derivative asBNB and yield-bearing stablecoin USDF.

Aster’s roadmap includes zero-knowledge proofs, a purpose-built Layer 1 blockchain, and an intent-based system that simplifies trading by automating execution across chains and liquidity sources.

[NextHow to login to Aster with your wallet](https://docs.asterdex.com/overview/what-is-aster/how-to-login-to-aster-with-your-wallet)

# How to login to Aster with your wallet | Aster

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/overview/what-is-aster/how-to-login-to-aster-with-your-wallet#how-to-connect-your-wallet-to-aster)

How to connect your wallet to Aster?

1.  Go to [https://www.asterdex.com/en](https://www.asterdex.com/en)
     or find the app in your wallet. Click \[Launch app\] or \[Trade Now\].
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FvE7E7j5N5y2HwIGoMibb%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-03-31%252015.29.54.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd55cb64e-e9e9-47f8-ac35-1deeb10761b2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6301895f&sv=2)

1.  Select a chain from the dropdown menu and click \[Connect wallet\].
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FHvrHynSXyfROjO7d8lOp%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-03-31%252015.32.30.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9678c7de-d88f-4ca5-8f89-22b282461059&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5d642c12&sv=2)

1.  Aster supports the MetaMask Wallet and Binance Wallet extensions. You can also click on \[WalletConnect\] to connect dozens of other supported Web3 wallets.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FHRklRpUJ0cxMNn5YvCdz%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-03-31%252015.34.06.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D35a441f0-acdc-42f4-811b-0af8b911d62a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=aae8ebd&sv=2)

1.  You will receive a sign message request. Click \[Send request\]. After signing in your wallet, you're connected. _Note: You need to hold at least 0.001 BNB in your wallet if you are connecting to BNB Chain._
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252F0Jqp95GDz5GWqWnj4k0e%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-03-31%252015.35.11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0baa5877-d13d-4d5c-9785-e26be96bd200&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f3d60a83&sv=2)

# How to login to Aster with your email address | Aster

Aster now supports email login for your convenience. All you need is a valid email address and you will be able to use Aster products after depositing funds.

Currently, only USDT deposits on the Arbitrum network is supported for email login.

**How-to guide**

1.  Go to [https://www.asterdex.com/en](https://www.asterdex.com/en)
    . Click \[Launch app\] or \[Trade Now\].
    
    ![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FvE7E7j5N5y2HwIGoMibb%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-03-31%252015.29.54.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd55cb64e-e9e9-47f8-ac35-1deeb10761b2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6301895f&sv=2)
    
2.  Click \[Connect\] button on the top right corner and enter your email address.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FFX90RN6IBSmWgfNshJ1n%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1d3734ee-6796-4f3c-ae2c-d8762cf7326d&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4f5ad4c&sv=2)

1.  After you submit your email address, a 6 digit code will be sent to your email. Type in the 6 digit code to login.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FklALIyYeKiaKPkDP8i54%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0a874fda-ede4-4243-a5a9-42f453ebc943&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=96fcd680&sv=2)

1.  Create and enter a strong password for your Aster login.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FkVwhIJM7LotV3rUb7tyN%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5417b130-47ed-4892-b693-7aa9d5577304&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8b07f672&sv=2)

1.  Sign the popup message after and continue to get started with Aster.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252Fjr0znpjA9dkU9bNihjiX%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7fb935e5-a271-46ac-9e5c-ffdd87846c0f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a3ff679b&sv=2)

1.  A new blockchain address has been created for your email address. All you need to do now is deposit funds to get started - click the \[Deposit\] button after clicking your wallet address button on the top right corner.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252F7m0VvP8x2grNNWCsd950%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8b953ebb-63e0-4e3d-830f-ac3673c695f8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2961679c&sv=2)

1.  Deposit your collateral from your DeFi wallet or Centralized Exchange (CEX) based on the supported networks. **Please take note that you can only deposit USDT via** [**Arbitrum One**](https://arbitrum.io/)
     **chain to your newly created wallet via email login. Aster is not liable for refunds if you have deposited the wrong asset on the wrong network.**
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FCT1mmyG7EXvo1a6iHKPB%252FFrame%25201312315515.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D70ed51d4-e1fc-44b0-ba71-d259b00095a6&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d0e9f485&sv=2)

1.  Once your wallet address tied to your email address has received USDT on Arbitrum, you can start using the asset as collateral to trade on Aster Pro.
    

[PreviousHow to login to Aster with your wallet](https://docs.asterdex.com/overview/what-is-aster/how-to-login-to-aster-with-your-wallet)

# How to retrieve your wrong deposit assets by Email log on Aster | Aster

if you deposit the wrong tokens like USDC rather than USDT on the ARBITRUM network. Please follow the guidance to retrieve your tokens.

1.  Go to [https://www.asterdex.com/en](https://www.asterdex.com/en)
    . Click \[Launch app\] or \[Trade Now\].
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FCAn6ve3eGK8ROQCINim3%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-10-13%252023.22.12.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D143661cb-5fff-4a5a-883e-3850580b7d07&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=52772782&sv=2)

1.  Click the \[Connect\] button on the top right corner and enter your email address.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FIBf5dmPZ9UxUVc0Wls8a%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-10-13%252023.23.15.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4a1337e3-57e1-461d-8c1f-94f6346ab388&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2e3f6453&sv=2)

1.  Click the \[Withdraw\] button and check the third point.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FVjGpcmD6r7siK1K0Xebn%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-11-03%252011.39.38.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dac902146-ce03-4dcf-a790-0b04682e2f34&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e1e3900b&sv=2)

1.  Select the blockchain (BNB, ETH &ARB) and token, input your destination address and click \[Transfer\] button to retrieve your tokens.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252F2A9i3JRezTvCU8ccYerW%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-11-03%252011.41.41.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D915cacd9-2ceb-4cf6-8f39-75bf479ada46&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1d8c9303&sv=2)

**Important Note:**

Users are responsible for paying gas fees when withdrawing unsupported assets from email-linked wallet to their wallet - please make sure you have these corresponding tokens to pay gas fees for these networks:

1.  BSC network: _BNB token_
    
2.  Ethereum and Arbitrum networks: _Ethereum token_

# Our smart contracts | Aster

Aster’s smart contracts are the foundation of our decentralized platform. Designed for security and transparency, they enable everything from perpetual trading to earn products.

This page lists the official Aster smart contract addresses across supported networks for your reference.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/overview/what-is-aster/our-smart-contracts#aster-treasury-contract)

**Aster Treasury Contract**

*   **BNB Chain:** 0x128463A60784c4D3f46c23Af3f65Ed859Ba87974
    
*   **Ethereum:** 0x604DD02d620633Ae427888d41bfd15e38483736E
    
*   **Solana:** EhUtRgu9iEbZXXRpEvDj6n1wnQRjMi2SERDo3c6bmN2c
    
*   **Arbitrum:** 0x9E36CB86a159d479cEd94Fa05036f235Ac40E1d5
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/overview/what-is-aster/our-smart-contracts#asterearn)

# Deposit & withdraw guide | Aster

In [Aster Pro](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/v1/BTCUSDT)

An example of a negative balance

# Aster Perpetual (Pro) | Aster

[**Aster Pro**](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/v1/BTCUSDT)
 is Aster’s decentralized perpetual contracts product and the core of our platform. It’s designed to offer traders greater control, deeper functionality, and a range of tools to support advanced strategies. Pro mode is available on BNB Chain, Ethereum, Solana, and Arbitrum.

This section covers everything you need to use Pro effectively — including trading mechanics, margin systems, risk management tools, and more.

**Key features include:**

*   **Multi-asset mode**: Trade using a variety of cryptocurrencies as margin. [Learn more](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/asterex-pro-mode/muti-single-asset-margin)
    
*   **Lower-than-CEX fees**: 0.01% maker fee, 0.035% taker fee

# Auto-deleveraging | Aster

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#what-is-adl)

What is ADL?

Auto-Deleveraging (ADL) is a risk management mechanism that activates during extreme market conditions. It’s used only when other protective systems (like liquidation and insurance) cannot cover losses in time.

While Aster aims to minimize the chances of ADL occurring, understanding how it works can help traders prepare and manage their risk.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#how-does-adl-work)

How does ADL work?

When a position is liquidated but the execution price is worse than the bankruptcy price (the price at which a trader’s losses equal their collateral, meaning their margin balance is zero), the system absorbs the remaining loss.

However, if the liquidation can’t be completed before the mark price hits the bankruptcy price, the system triggers ADL. This forcibly reduces the size of opposite-side positions held by other traders, starting with those who are most profitable and highly leveraged.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#how-adl-priority-is-determined)

How ADL priority is determined

The system uses a ranking system based on a trader’s profit and leverage. This determines the order in which users are affected if ADL is triggered.

Here’s how the system calculates the ADL priority:

1.  **PnL percent**
    
    max(0, Unrealized profit) ÷ max(1, Wallet balance)
    
2.  **Margin ratio**
    
    If (Wallet balance + Unrealized profit) ≤ 0:
    
    → margin ratio = 0
    
    If (Wallet balance + Unrealized profit) > 0:
    
    → Margin ratio = Maintenance margin ÷ (Wallet balance + Unrealized profit)
    
3.  **Leverage PnL**
    
    PnL percent × Margin ratio
    
4.  **Leverage PnL quantile**
    
    User's leverage PnL rank ÷ Total number of users
    

The higher your leverage PnL quantile, the higher your ADL risk.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#adl-risk-indicator)

ADL risk indicator

In AsterEX Pro mode, the LeveragePnLQuantile bar shows your risk of being auto-deleveraged:

*   4 bars = high ADL risk
    
*   Fewer bars = lower ADL risk
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FVUhltNkjAciejKmuGNav%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-04-01%252009.38.59.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D91f523a9-1acc-4918-923d-d6a9ebd73cf9&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c4f4100b&sv=2)

This position is showing 1 of 4 bars - there is a low ADL risk

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#how-to-reduce-adl-risk)

How to reduce ADL risk

*   Lower your leverage
    
*   Close and reopen your position to reset your priority in the ADL queue
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#what-happens-if-youre-adld)

What happens if you’re ADL’d

*   Your position is partially or fully reduced without warning
    
*   You can re-enter the market at any time after
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging#additional-notes)

Additional notes

*   The bankruptcy price might fall outside the current trading range, making it harder to fully close your position before losses exceed your margin
    
*   ADL mostly affects traders with high leverage and large unrealized profits

[NextFees](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/fees)

# Margin | Aster

Margin trading on Aster Pro lets you amplify your positions by borrowing funds, allowing you to trade with more size than your actual balance.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin#leverage)

Leverage

Leverage lets you open a larger position with a smaller amount of collateral (margin). For example, with 10× leverage, a $100 margin allows you to open a $1,000 position.

You can choose your desired leverage using the slider or input field in the trading panel. Each asset has its own maximum limit.

The initial margin required to open a position is based on your leverage. It’s calculated using the formula: (Position size × Mark price) / Leverage

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin#margin-modes)

Margin modes

Aster Pro supports two margin modes:

*   **Cross margin (default)** Your margin is shared across all open positions. Profits from one trade can offset losses in another. This reduces liquidation risk but puts your entire margin balance at stake.
    
*   **Isolated margin** Margin is applied to a single position. If the trade moves against you, only the margin tied to that position is at risk. Other positions remain unaffected.
    

You can select the margin mode directly in the trading interface (**Cross**/**Isolated**) before opening a position. You cannot change the margin mode after you’ve submitted a position or opened an order.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin#monitoring-margin)

Monitoring margin

You can track your **used margin**, **liquidation price**, and **available balance** in real time within the position panel. This helps you manage risk and avoid liquidation.

Maintenance margin is the **minimum amount required to keep a position open**. If your margin falls below this level, your position may be liquidated. It's based on the **total size** of your position, not the leverage you select. As position size increases, higher portions fall into higher **maintenance margin tiers**, each with progressively higher rates.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin#liquidation)

Liquidation

If your margin falls below the maintenance requirement, your position may be liquidated to prevent further losses. Keeping an eye on your margin ratio and funding rates is key to staying safe.

[PreviousCosts of opening positions](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/costs-of-opening-positions)
[NextCalculating max transfers in Cross and Isolated margin](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin/calculating-max-transfers-in-cross-and-isolated-margin)

# Fees | Aster

**Fee rates:**

*   **Maker fee**: 0.005%
    
    *   A **Maker** order is one that **adds liquidity** to the order book. When you place a Maker order, you choose a price **above or below the current market price**, and your order **is not filled immediately**. Instead, it sits on the order book, waiting for another trader to match and fill it. You’re essentially making the market by placing an order that helps set available prices for others to trade.
        
    
*   **Taker fee**: 0.04%
    
    *   A **Taker** order is one that **removes liquidity** from the order book. When you place a Taker order, you’re trading **immediately** against an existing Maker order at the current available price. You're _taking_ liquidity by accepting someone else’s open order.
        
    

**How to use $ASTER to pay perpetual trading fees and get a 5% discount**

You can save 5% on perpetual trading fees when you pay with $ASTER. Simply deposit $ASTER into your perp wallet, and it will automatically be used to cover fees. You can also transfer $ASTER from your spot account to your perpetual account to enjoy the discount.

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/fees#how-are-fees-calculated)

🔍 How are fees calculated?

In AsterEX Pro Mode, transaction fees are based on the **nominal value** of your order — that is, the total value of the position you're opening or closing.

**Formula:**

*   **Transaction fee** = Nominal value × Fee rate
    
*   **Nominal value** = Number of contracts × Transaction price
    
    *   **Number of contracts**: Each contract typically represents a unit of the base asset — for example, 1 BTC in BTCUSDT contracts. So if you're trading 0.1 BTC, that’s 0.1 contracts.
        
    *   **Transaction price**: The price at which the trade happens (e.g. $80,000 for 1 BTC).
        
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/fees#example-1-market-buy-taker-order)

🧮 Example 1: Market buy (Taker order)

You place a **market order** to buy **0.1 BTC** at **$80,000**.

*   **Nominal value** = 0.1 × 80,000 = 8,000
    
*   **Transaction fee** = 8,000 × 0.04% = 3.2 **USDT**
    

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/fees#example-2-limit-sell-maker-order)

🧮 Example 2: Limit sell (Maker order)

Later, you place a **limit sell order** at **$85,000**.

*   **Nominal value** = 0.1 × 85,000 = 8,500
    
*   **Transaction fee** = 8,500 × 0.005% = **0.425 USDT**

[NextFunding rate](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate)

# Funding rate | Aster

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate#what-is-the-funding-rate)

What is the funding rate?

In perpetual futures contracts, the funding rate is a periodic payment exchanged between traders holding long and short positions. This mechanism helps ensure that the contract price stays close to the underlying spot market price.

*   Positive funding rate: When the contract price is above the mark price, long traders pay short traders.
    
*   Negative funding rate: When the contract price is below the mark price, short traders pay long traders.
    

This payment encourages traders to take positions that push the contract price back in line with the spot price.

Note: There is a 15-second deviation between the actual time and the time the funding fee is taken. For example, if you open a position at 16:00:05 UTC, you may still be charged a funding fee. Therefore, it is important that you pay attention to the exact time you open a position.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate#funding-rate-formula)

Funding rate formula

Funding rate = Premium index + Interest rate

*   Premium index reflects the difference between the perpetual contract price and the spot price.
    
*   Interest rate is fixed at 0.03% per day on AsterEX.
    

For example, if the premium index is 0.015%, the total funding rate would be 0.045%.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate#premium-index-calculation)

Premium index calculation

Premium index = \[max(0, Impact bid price − Index price) − max(0, Index price − Impact ask price)\] ÷ Index price

Where:

*   Index price = Weighted average price from external spot exchanges
    
*   Impact bid price = Average price to sell a fixed notional value using the current bid depth
    
*   Impact ask price = Average price to buy a fixed notional value using the current ask depth
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate#how-to-calculate-impact-bid-price)

How to calculate impact bid price

To determine the Impact bid price, identify the level in the order book where the cumulative quote value exceeds the Impact Margin Notional (IMN).

To help visualize the calculation, the following table shows how quote notional values accumulate across levels in the order book:

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Flh7-rt.googleusercontent.com%2Fdocsz%2FAD_4nXcShRwPvPDsa0sKITn9DLRIkFrc7LuURl0dWTxxZbl7BdbFRvduOOvTWYSOTvZAY5tCjEtmYM9Aol5Jfa9j5uQAKJJVF_J_XUUes4ypB5E8Ed6lfWYnF-B68DCpiVsr3f-un-29Nw%3Fkey%3DJqn2SG7YdgNR0qh-IRD44Q&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d93e3091&sv=2)

In this table:

*   Quote Notional Quantity = price × quantity × contract multiplier
    
*   Accumulated Quote Notional Quantity is the sum of quote notional values up to that level.
    

Once the accumulated quote notional exceeds the IMN, the corresponding level is used in the final Impact Bid (or Ask) Price formula.

If:

Contract multiplier × ∑px × qx > IMN

and

Contract multiplier × ∑px-1 × qx-1 < IMN

Then level x is used to calculate the Impact Bid Price using: Impact Bid Price = IMN / \[(IMN − Contract Multiplier × ∑px−1 × qx−1) / px + Contract Multiplier × ∑qx−1\]

Where:

*   px = Price at level x
    
*   qx = Quantity at level x
    
*   IMN = Impact margin notional (predefined value)
    
*   Contract multiplier = Multiplier for the contract (usually 1)
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate#example-order-book-bid-side)

Example order book (bid side)

Assume the bid-side of the order book is:

Level

Price (px)

Quantity (qx)

1

100

5

2

99

10

3

98

15

To calculate the Impact Bid Price, accumulate quoted value by level until it meets or exceeds the IMN (Impact Margin Notional). Then apply the formula above using the correct level data.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate#funding-amount)

Funding amount

The funding amount is how much you will actually pay or receive based on the funding rate.

Funding amount = Position size × Mark price × Funding rate

This value is transferred between long and short traders depending on the direction of the funding rate. **Aster does not charge or receive funding** — it is a peer-to-peer transfer.

[NextCosts of opening positions](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/costs-of-opening-positions)

# Liquidations | Aster

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#understanding-liquidation-mechanics)

Understanding liquidation mechanics

In [Aster Pro](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/v1/BTCUSDT)
, liquidations are designed to protect both traders and the platform during periods of high volatility. Aster uses both the **last price** and the [**mark price**](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/asterex-pro/mark-price)
 to manage liquidation processes effectively:

*   **Last price**: This is the most recent transaction price of a contract and is used to calculate realized profit and loss (PnL).​
    
*   **Mark price**: Calculated based on a combination of funding data and a basket of prices from multiple spot exchanges, the mark price is used to determine unrealized PnL and trigger liquidations.​
    

Risk and leverage are adjusted based on exposure; larger positions require higher margin and offer lower leverage.​

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#when-liquidation-occurs)

When liquidation occurs

A forced liquidation is triggered when:​

**Margin = Initial Collateral + Realized PnL + Unrealized PnL < Maintenance margin**​

To avoid liquidation (i.e., when the risk ratio hits 100%), it's recommended to maintain a margin ratio below 80% by adding sufficient margin or reducing the position size.​

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#forced-liquidation-price)

Forced liquidation price

Forced liquidation occurs when the mark price reaches the liquidation price. Monitoring both the mark price and your liquidation price is crucial to prevent unwanted liquidations.​

In **cross margin** mode with hedge trading, both long and short positions of the same contract share the same liquidation price. In **isolated margin** mode, long and short positions have different liquidation prices based on the margin allocated to each.​

A built-in future calculator to compute liquidation prices is coming soon.​

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#forced-liquidation-process)

Forced liquidation process

When your margin falls below the maintenance requirement, the system initiates forced liquidation to limit further losses and protect the platform.

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#what-happens-during-liquidation)

What happens during liquidation:

*   All open orders on your account are immediately canceled.
    
*   A single large [**Immediate-or-Cancel (IOC)** order](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/asterex-pro/order-types#time-in-force-tif-options)
     is submitted to reduce your position size. The system attempts to fill as much as possible and cancel the rest.
    
*   If your margin is sufficient after this step—accounting for realized losses and liquidation fees—liquidation stops.
    
*   If not, your remaining position is closed at the **bankruptcy price**, and the position is handed over to the **insurance fund**. Your account is then marked as **bankrupt**.
    

If your wallet balance becomes negative at this point, the insurance fund covers the loss and pays any outstanding fees. Any remaining assets (if applicable) are also allocated to the insurance fund.

Additional notes:

*   Different liquidation protocols may apply depending on your position’s size and risk level, helping to minimize the chance of full liquidation.
    
*   It’s advisable to close positions manually before approaching the maintenance margin threshold to avoid forced liquidation fees.
    
*   Smaller positions are generally more likely to be fully liquidated, as they have less margin buffer and may not qualify for partial liquidation. Larger positions benefit from margin tiering, which allows for more gradual risk reduction.
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#liquidation-settlement-and-negative-balance-handling)

Liquidation settlement and negative balance handling

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#automatic-negative-balance-settlement)

Automatic negative balance settlement

If your account ends up with a **negative balance after liquidation**, Aster may use funds from the **insurance fund** to cover the loss — but only under specific conditions.

To qualify for **automatic settlement**, all of the following must apply:

*   The negative balance is in a **USDT perpetuals** account.
    
*   The account has **no open positions** (cross or isolated margin).
    
*   The negative balance is **no greater than 5,000 USDT**.
    
*   **No funds have been transferred** into the account after liquidation to offset the loss.
    

If you meet these conditions, the settlement will be handled automatically. If not, please contact us via [Discord](https://discord.gg/invite/asterdefi)
 for further assistance.

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations#liquidation-settlement-fee)

Liquidation settlement fee

When your position is liquidated, a portion of the **liquidation fee** is allocated to the insurance fund. This appears in your transaction history as an **“Insurance Clearance Fee”**.

You can find more details on fee tiers in the Trading Rules page.

Additional notes:

*   Bankruptcy prices may fall outside the contract’s current market range.
    
*   Due to latency or syncing issues, some numerical values may update without notice.
    

[PreviousMark price](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/mark-price)
[NextAuto-deleveraging](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/auto-deleveraging)

Last updated 2 months ago

# Mark price | Aster

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/mark-price#overview)

**Overview**

On [Aster Pro](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/v1/BTCUSDT)
, the **mark price** serves as a reference price to calculate traders' unrealized profit and loss (PnL). It helps reduce unnecessary forced [liquidations](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/asterex-pro/liquidations)
 during periods of abnormal market volatility, ensuring fair and accurate pricing of perpetual contracts.​

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/mark-price#price-index)

**Price index**

The **price index** is a weighted average derived from major spot markets such as Binance, Huobi, and Kraken. Markets with higher trading volumes have a greater influence on the index value. This index represents the fair value of the asset's spot price and is used to calculate the mark price, which is crucial for determining unrealized PnL.​

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/mark-price#mark-price-calculation)

**Mark price calculation**

The mark price is determined by taking the median of three prices:​

*   **Price 1**: Price index × (1 + Funding rate × (Time to next funding rate in hours ÷ 8))
    
*   **Price 2**: Price index + 5-minute moving average
    
*   **Contract Price**: The current contract price​
    

The **5-minute moving average** is calculated by sampling every minute over a 5-minute interval:​

Moving average = Average of ((bid 1 + ask 1) ÷ 2 − Price index)​

The **mark price** is the median of Price 1, Price 2, and the Contract Price. For example, if Price 1 < Price 2 < Contract Price, then Price 2 is selected as the Mark Price.​

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/mark-price#handling-abnormal-market-conditions)

**Handling abnormal market conditions**

In cases of significant deviations between price sources or abnormal market conditions causing large differences between the spot price and the mark price, Aster Pro may implement precautionary measures:​

*   **Single price source deviation**: If the last price from a particular exchange deviates more than 5% from the median price of all sources, that exchange's price weight is set to zero.
    
*   **Multiple price source deviations**: If more than one exchange shows a deviation greater than 5%, the median price of all sources is used as the index value instead of the weighted average.
    
*   **Exchange connectivity issues:** If any exchange fails to update its price feed within 3 seconds, that source is removed from the price index calculation. This prevents outdated prices from influencing the mark price.
    
*   **Last trade price protection:** If the latest trade price deviates more than 5% from the mark price and no new trade occurs within 5 seconds, the contract price is replaced with the current mark price in the mark price calculation. This prevents the system from using stale or potentially manipulated trade prices in liquidation-related processes.
    

[PreviousFees & Specs](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs)
[NextLiquidations](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/liquidations)

# Calculating max transfers in Cross and Isolated margin | Aster

When using Cross or Isolated Margin modes, the amount you can transfer in or out depends on your wallet balance, margin requirements, and unrealized profit and loss. Here’s how to calculate it.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin/calculating-max-transfers-in-cross-and-isolated-margin#cross-margin)

Cross margin

In Cross Margin mode, your margin balance is shared across all open positions. The maximum amount you can transfer out depends on your wallet balance, unrealized PnL, and the required margin for open orders.

**If there is no unrealized PnL:**

Maximum transferable amount = Cross wallet balance − Σ(Isolated open order initial margin) − Σ(Cross position maintenance margin)

**If there is unrealized PnL:**

Maximum transferable amount = Cross wallet balance + Σ(Cross unrealized PnL) − Σ(Cross initial margin) − Σ(Isolated open order initial margin)

Note: These calculations assume no gift balance or cross collateral.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin/calculating-max-transfers-in-cross-and-isolated-margin#isolated-margin)

Isolated margin

In Isolated Margin mode, margin is dedicated to each individual position. The maximum amount you can transfer in or out depends on the available margin relative to that position’s maintenance requirements.

**Maximum transfer-in amount for Isolated Margin:**

Maximum transfer-in amount = min (Cross wallet balance − Σ(Isolated open position initial margin) − Σ(Cross position maintenance margin), Available balance)

**Maximum transfer-out amount for Isolated Margin:**

Maximum transfer-out amount = max (0, min (Isolated wallet balance − Isolated position maintenance margin,

Isolated wallet balance + Size × (Mark price − Entry price) − Mark price × Abs(Size) × Initial margin rate))

Note:

*   Transferring margin out reduces the buffer protecting your position.
    
*   Removing too much margin can increase your risk of liquidation.
    

[PreviousMargin](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin)
[NextSingle asset mode & Multi-asset mode](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/single-asset-mode-and-multi-asset-mode)

# Costs of opening positions | Aster

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/costs-of-opening-positions#how-we-calculate-the-cost-of-opening-a-limit-order)

How we calculate the cost of opening a Limit Order

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FJTyqvfSaBSxOInewx3Yl%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-05-09%252010.02.11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da583a464-85b6-43d2-938b-4bf946807f3e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=737d03a4&sv=2)

1.  **Calculate the initial margin**
    

Initial margin

\= Notional Value / Leverage Multiplier

\= (102,990.0\*1 BTC)/20x

\= 5,149.50

1.  **Calculate open loss**
    

Open Loss = Number of Contracts × Absolute Value {min \[0, Order Direction × (Mark Price — Order Price)\]}

Direction of order: 1 for long order; -1 for short order

Open loss of long orders:

\= Number of Contract \* Absolute Value {min\[0, Direction of order \* (Mark price — Order Price)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, 1 \* (102,988.4- 102,990.0)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, (-1.6)\]}

\= 1 \* 1.6

\= 1.6

Open loss occurs when you place a long order.

Open loss of short orders:

\= Number of Contract \* Absolute Value {min\[0, Direction of order \* (Mark Price — Order Price)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, -1 \* (102,988.4- 102,990.0)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, 1.6\]}

\= 1 \* 0

\= 0

Open loss does not occur when you place a short order.

1.  **Calculate the cost of opening a position**
    

Since there is no open loss when you place a short order, the cost of opening a short order is equal to the initial margin.

Cost of opening a long order:

\= 5,149.50+ 1.6

\= 5,151.1

Cost of opening a short order

\= 5,149.50 + 0

\= 5,149.50

Since placing a long order results in an open loss, it requires more margin than a short order. In addition to the initial margin, you must also take into account the open loss.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/costs-of-opening-positions#how-we-calculate-the-cost-of-opening-a-market-order)

How we calculate the cost of opening a Market Order

1.  **Calculate estimated entry price**
    

Long order estimated entry price = ask\[0\] \* (1 + 0.05%); Short order estimated entry price = max(bid\[0\], mark price)

*   Estimated entry price of long orders
    

\= ask\[0\]\*(1 + 0.05%)

\= 102,946.8\*(1 + 0.05%)

\= 102,998.27

\*\[0\]：Level 1 price

*   Assuming price of short orders
    

\= max(bid\[0\], mark price)

\= max (102,946.9, 102,941.0)

\= 102,946.9

\*\[0\]：Level 1 price

1.  **Calculate the initial margin**
    

Initial Margin = Notional Value / Leverage Multiplier

*   Initial margin for long orders
    

\= Estimated entry price of long order \* Number of Contracts / Leverage Multiplier

\= 102,998.27 \* 1 /20

\= 5,149.9135

*   Initial margin for short orders
    

\= Estimated entry price of short order \* Number of Contracts / Leverage Multiplier

\= 102,946.9 \* 1/20

\= 5,147.345

1.  **Calculate the open loss**
    

Open Loss = Number of Contract \* Absolute Value {min\[0, direction of order \* (mark price — order price)\]}

Direction of order: 1 for long order; -1 for short order

*   Open loss for long order
    

\= Number of Contract \* Absolute Value {min\[0, direction of order \* (mark price — order price)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, 1 \* (102,941.0–102,998.27)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, -57.27\]}

\= 1 \* 57.27

\= 57.27

An open loss occurs when you place a long order.

*   Open loss for short order
    

\= Number of Contract \* Absolute Value {min\[0, direction of order \* (mark price — order price)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, -1 \* (102,941.0–102,946.9)\]}

\= 1 \* Absolute Value {min\[0, 5.9\]}

\= 1 \* 0

\= 0

An open loss does not occur when you place a short order.

1.  **Calculating the cost of opening a position**
    

Since open loss occurs when you place a long order, it costs more to place a long order. In addition to the initial margin, you must also take into account the open loss.

*   Cost of opening a long order
    

\= 5,149.9135+57.27

\= 5,207.1835

*   Cost of opening a short order
    

\= 5,147.345+0

\= 5,147.345

Since there is no open loss when you place a short order, the cost of opening a short order is equal to the initial margin.

[PreviousFunding rate](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/fees-and-specs/funding-rate)
[NextMargin](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/margin)

Last updated 4 months ago

# Hidden Order | Aster

A hidden order is a type of order that allows traders to place a limit order without revealing any information about its size or presence to the public order book.

Unlike visible orders, hidden orders are completely concealed from other market participants, ensuring privacy and discretion. They operate within the existing order book, sharing liquidity with other orders, which helps maintain tight spreads and efficient price discovery.

For example, a trader might place a hidden buy order for Bitcoin at $500,000. Nothing appears on the order book about this order — only if another trader sells into this hidden order will it be filled, at which point the trade becomes publicly visible.

Since hidden orders are designed to protect a trader’s intended price point, they often execute faster than iceberg orders and prevent market prices from moving in reaction to the order’s presence.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/order-types/hidden-order#why-use-hidden-orders-compared-to-traditional-orders)

Why use hidden orders? Compared to traditional orders

Normal Order

Hidden Order

**Shows on order book**

Yes

No

**Price impact**

No

Minimal market price impact

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/order-types/hidden-order#hidden-orders-compared-to-similar-order-types)

Hidden orders compared to similar order types

Hidden Order

Iceberg Order

Dark Pools

**Invisible**

Yes

No (partially visible)

Yes

**Anonymous**

Yes

Yes

Yes

**Minimal market**

**price impact**

Yes

No

Yes

**Liquid markets**

Yes

Yes

No

Traders utilize hidden orders to achieve **stealth execution**, **reduce market impact**, and access **deep liquidity** without revealing their trading intentions. In fast-paced, highly leveraged markets like crypto perpetual futures, they offer a strategic advantage by enabling smooth and discreet trading.

Unlike dark pools, which fragment liquidity, or iceberg orders, which partially reveal intent, hidden orders provide full anonymity while still allowing traders to tap into the liquidity available in the public order book.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/order-types/hidden-order#tutorial-how-to-place-a-hidden-order-on-aster-pro)

Tutorial: How to place a Hidden Order on Aster Pro

1.  After connecting your wallet to [Aster Pro](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/v1/BTCUSDT)
    , select your preferred contract, leverage, and order amount. Click the checkbox \[Hidden Order\]. Hidden orders are automatically limit orders.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252F8MZ5PwWqpxN5ShAtKi49%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-06-20%252018.03.07.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dacfbeb1f-fb66-44f3-8d8d-a804a796fcd5&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a49dc4cd&sv=2)

1.  Your order will appear under \[Open orders\] but will not appear in the public order book. You can differentiate a hidden order from a normal order via the not-visible icon.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252Fp0wALsRRUPspFjHg19zJ%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-06-20%252018.05.41.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3a000dc9-0efb-4fa8-a604-d875f374c0b3&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fc97b72c&sv=2)

1.  The price and size of your hidden order is only disclosed after the trade is executed. Your trade will then be reflected under \[Positions\].
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FLFlAuOqmPhYDyRnNa39M%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-06-20%252018.07.13.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd3bc54e9-995f-4814-a68b-271fe5ef9416&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9b8e93c2&sv=2)

# VIP Program | Aster

_**Important notice**_: _Aster VIP Program will be updated to include_ _**$ASTER holding requirements on 3rd Nov at 00:00 UTC.**_

In appreciation of our users' continued support, Aster is introducing the VIP program to reward all our valued users by offering exclusive benefits and privileges.

Your VIP status is determined based on your rolling **14-day trading volume either in Spot or Perpetual (USD) and ASTER holding balance**, assessed daily at the **end of each UTC day**. To qualify as a VIP, you need to meet both the trading volume and holding balance requirements.

As a VIP member, you will enjoy reduced fees for Spot and Futures trading, making your trading experience more rewarding.

Please refer to the image below for detailed VIP requirements and fee benefits.

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FI3Wmi1D5MoM6Y5uiEVfa%252FAster%2520VIP%2520Program%2520Update%2520%282%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D25354bff-45b9-40c1-81c4-2831625aa5c5&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=580d8501&sv=2)

**Aster holding balance Calculation Mechanism**

Daily Average ASTER Balance will include both ASTER tokens held in Aster Spot account and Perpetual account. Check the detailed calculation formula as below:

Total Daily Average ASTER Balance = Sum of the daily averages of the following:

*   Spot total ASTER Balance
    
*   Perpetual ASTER Wallet Balance
    

Note:

*   Daily Average Spot Account Balance is calculated using the sum of the hourly snapshots of ASTER balance in the spot account in a day divided by 24 (hours).
    
*   Daily Average Aster Perpetual Wallet Balance is calculated as the sum of the hourly snapshots of the ASTER balance in the Aster Futures Account in a day divided by 24 (hours).
    

This update to the ASTER balance calculation mechanism will impact the following aspects of the Aster Ecosystem:

*   VIP program
    

Please note that:

*   Each day runs from 00:00:00 (UTC) to 23:59:59 (UTC).
    
*   Hourly snapshots will occur at random times.
    
*   Pending orders are included in the balance calculation.

[NextAster Earn](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-earn)

# Dumb mode | Aster

Dumb mode is a forecast-based trading feature on [Aster Simple](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/BTCUSD)
 that allows users to predict minute-by-minute price movements of an underlying asset. Trades are settled based on the asset’s entry and expiry prices.

This mode is available on both **BNB Chain** and **Arbitrum** networks.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/dumb-mode#how-to-place-dumb-mode-orders)

How to place Dumb mode orders

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FdNpLtyoXjlBN4vGQbNdQ%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-04-21%252016.04.08.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7f35524c-44cc-463d-baac-1168db00290b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c17bee81&sv=2)

Choosing the expiration period

1.  Toggle to Dumb mode:
    
    *   Switch between **Perp** and **Dumb** modes. Ensure you’re in Dumb mode.
        
    
2.  Select asset and expiration period:
    
    *   Choose the desired asset and set the expiration duration.
        
    *   Available expiration windows:
        
        *   30 minutes: Maximum ROI of 72%.
            
        *   1 hour: Maximum ROI of 77%.
            
        *   For BTC/USD and ETH/USD:
            
            *   5 minutes: Maximum ROI of 77%.
                
            *   15 minutes: Maximum ROI of 80%.
                
            *   30 minutes: Maximum ROI of 82%.
                
            
        
    
3.  Place a bet (open position):
    
    *   Choose a default percentage setting or manually input the principal amount.
        
    

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/dumb-mode#important-notes)

Important notes:

*   Expiration timer:
    
    *   The countdown begins after the transaction is confirmed on the blockchain, not when the 'Long' or 'Short' button is clicked.
        
    
*   Entry price reference:
    
    *   The displayed entry price is for reference only. The actual entry price is determined at the moment the transaction is confirmed on the blockchain.
        
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/dumb-mode#profit-and-loss-conditions)

Profit and loss conditions

*   Long position:
    
    *   If the expiry price > entry price: You make a profit (subject to performance adjustments)
        
    *   If the expiry price ≤ entry price: You lose your entire principal
        
    
*   Short position:
    
    *   If the expiry price < entry price: You make a profit (subject to performance adjustments)
        
    *   If the expiry price ≥ entry price: You lose your entire principal
        
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/dumb-mode#fees)

Fees

*   No open/close fees are charged in Dumb Mode.
    
*   A 6% fee on the principal is applied only on winning trades. This fee is already factored into the ROI.
    

[PreviousDegen mode](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/degen-mode)
[NextManage your positions](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/manage-your-positions)

# Price oracles | Aster

[1001x](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/BTCUSD)
 utilizes a robust and decentralized oracle system to provide accurate and real-time price feeds for trading pairs. This system aggregates data from multiple reputable sources to ensure price integrity and protect users from anomalies.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/price-oracles#data-sources)

Data sources

*   **Primary source**: Pyth Oracle’s price feed serves as the anchor
    
*   **Verification**: Prices are cross-verified with Chainlink’s price feed
    
*   **Fallback**: For trading pairs not supported by Pyth Oracle, Binance Oracle is used as a backup
    

If Pyth Oracle’s price deviates by more than 1% from Chainlink’s price, a circuit breaker is triggered, causing the transaction to fail.

All trading pairs on 1001x use the oracle price of the listed assets as the index price.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/price-oracles#how-prices-are-fetched-and-verified)

How prices are fetched and verified

1.  On-chain request: When a trader initiates a transaction, a request for the latest price is simultaneously triggered.
    
2.  Off-chain aggregation: Pyth Oracle retrieves the latest price and updates the index-weighted average price feed.
    
3.  On-chain verification: 1001x’s smart contracts compare Pyth’s price with Chainlink’s feed to verify data accuracy.
    
4.  Transaction completion: Once verification is successful, the trader’s transaction is executed.
    

This decentralized validation process ensures there is no single point of failure and typically completes within two blocks. Additional safeguards are in place to mitigate issues arising from market disruptions or connectivity problems.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/price-oracles#protective-measures)

Protective measures

*   Single source deviation: If an exchange’s last price deviates more than 5% from the median price of all sources, its weight is set to zero in calculations.
    
*   Multiple sources deviation: If multiple exchanges show deviations greater than 5%, the median price of all sources is used as the index value instead of a weighted average.
    
*   Connectivity issues:
    
    *   If an exchange’s data feed is inaccessible but had trades updated in the last 10 seconds, the latest available price data is used for index calculation.
        
    *   If no trade data has been updated for 10 seconds, the exchange’s weight is set to zero in the weighted average calculation.
        
    

[PreviousLeverage](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/leverage)
[NextFees & slippage](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/fees-and-slippage)

# Manage your positions | Aster

On [1001x](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/BTCUSD)
, all positions are isolated. This means each position uses its own margin, and losses are limited to that position only.

You can track and adjust your open positions directly in the app.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/manage-your-positions#view-your-positions)

View your positions

The position panel displays all open positions associated with your connected address. Each row includes:

*   Trading pair (e.g. BTC/USD)
    
*   Position direction (long or short)
    
*   Position size
    
*   Entry price
    
*   Mark price
    
*   Liquidation price
    
*   Estimated PnL
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/manage-your-positions#close-a-position)

Close a position

To close a position, click Close on the position row.

This will place a market order in the opposite direction of your current position and fully close it. For example:

*   A long position of 1 ETH will trigger a market sell of 1 ETH
    
*   A short position of 1 BTC will trigger a market buy of 1 BTC
    

You can also partially close a position by adjusting the order size before confirming.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/manage-your-positions#edit-margin)

Edit margin

If your leverage is below 500×, you can add margin to your open position at any time by clicking on the "+" icon. This can reduce your liquidation risk.

Note: Adding margin is not supported for positions using 500× leverage or higher.

[PreviousDumb mode](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/dumb-mode)
[NextOrder types](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/order-types)

# Leverage | Aster

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/leverage#what-is-leverage)

What is leverage?

Leverage enables you to control a larger position size than your actual wallet balance. For instance, with 5× leverage, a $1,000 margin allows you to open a $5,000 position. While this can magnify profits, it also increases potential losses.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/leverage#adjusting-your-leverage)

Adjusting your leverage

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FwOddeDaavsGMgf4iTye1%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deac6c664-5ed9-451d-92f4-c26a395be65a&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d733e342&sv=2)

BTC/USD's max leverage is 1,001x

You can manually set your leverage before opening a position, ranging from 1× up to 1001×, depending on the specific market.

*   **Increasing leverage**: Boosts your position size without additional margin but brings the liquidation price closer to your entry point.
    
*   **Decreasing leverage**: Reduces your position size and moves the liquidation price further from your entry, lowering risk.
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/leverage#leverage-and-position-management)

**Leverage and position management**

*   Leverages below 500×:
    
    *   You can add margin to open positions
        
    *   An open/close position fee of 0.08% applies
        
    
*   Leverages of 500× and above:
    
    *   Adding margin to open positions is not supported
        
    *   Maximum net profit ROI is capped:
        
        *   Approximately 500% for 500× and 750× leverage
            
        *   Approximately 300% for 1001× leverage
            
        
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/leverage#market-specific-leverage-and-fees)

**Market-specific leverage and fees**

*   BTCUSD:
    
    *   Up to 1001× leverage
        
    *   For 500×, 750×, and 1001× leverage:
        
        *   0% open position fee
            
        *   Lower price slippage
            
        *   A dynamic PnL fee is applied when closing positions. This fee is designed to charge fees based on profit and loss, aiming to protect traders from excessive losses.
            
        *   Adding margin to open positions is not supported
            
        *   Maximum net profit ROI:
            
            *   Approximately 500% for 500× and 750× leverage
                
            *   Approximately 300% for 1001× leverage
                
            
        
    *   For leverage below 500×:
        
        *   0.08% open/close position fees
            
        *   Margin can be added to open positions
            
        
    
*   ETH/USD:
    
    *   Up to 250× leverage
        
    *   0.08% open/close position fees
        
    *   Margin can be added to open positions
        
    
*   Other crypto perpetual contracts:
    
    *   Up to 75× leverage
        
    *   0.08% open/close position fees
        
    *   Margin can be added to open positions
        
    
*   Forex perpetual contracts:
    
    *   Up to 200× leverage
        
    *   0.02% open/close position fees
        
    *   Margin can be added to open positions
        
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/leverage#leverage-example)

**Leverage example**

Suppose you have $100 in your wallet and open a long BTC position at $20,000 using 10× leverage. Your position size becomes $1,000. If BTC’s price increases by 5% to $21,000, your profit is $50, yielding a 50% return on your $100 margin. By contrast, a 5% price drop would result in a 50% loss.

[NextPrice oracles](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/price-oracles)

# Single asset mode & Multi-asset mode | Aster

AsterEX Pro offers two margin modes to support different trading strategies:

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/single-asset-mode-and-multi-asset-mode#single-asset-mode)

Single-asset mode

*   **Collateral**: Only USDT is accepted.
    
*   **Margin allocation**: Margin is managed separately for each position.
    
*   **Risk management**: Each position is isolated — losses in one do not affect others.
    
*   **Profit and loss (PnL)**: PnL is calculated individually for each position.
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/single-asset-mode-and-multi-asset-mode#multi-asset-mode)

Multi-asset mode

*   **Collateral**: Supports a variety of cryptocurrencies, including restaked tokens.
    
*   **Margin allocation**: Margin is shared across all open positions, which helps you use capital more efficiently.
    
*   **Risk management**: Risk is evaluated across your entire portfolio, not position-by-position.
    
*   **Profit and loss (PnL)**: Gains and losses are netted across all open positions.
    
*   **Automatic balance management**:
    
    *   If the balance of a specific asset falls below a required threshold, the system automatically converts other assets in your wallet into the one that’s needed (e.g. converting ETH to USDT).
        
    *   This is done internally through the matching engine, with no additional commission.
        
    

**Note:** Multi-Asset Mode operates in cross margin only.

**Key benefits of multi-asset mode:**

*   **Efficient capital allocation**: Your margin is shared across positions, so you can use it more flexibly.
    
*   **Profitable setoff**: Gains from winning positions can offset losses from others in real-time.
    
*   **Simplified monitoring**: Your margin balance reflects net PnL, giving a clear view of your overall exposure.
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/single-asset-mode-and-multi-asset-mode#collateral-value-ratios)

Collateral value ratios

Each supported asset has a **collateral value ratio**, which determines how much of its value counts toward your usable margin. Assets with higher risk or volatility receive a larger discount.

What is 1,001x?

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple#key-features)

*   **Hedging strategies**: Implement techniques like delta-neutral strategies to manage risk and exposure effectively.​

    , [Chainlink](https://chain.link/)

# Order types | Aster

**Market order:** Executes immediately at the best available price in the order book. The final price depends on available liquidity. On Aster Spot, market orders are always considered taker trades because they consume liquidity.

**Limit order:** Lets traders set the maximum price they’re willing to pay when buying, or the minimum price they’re willing to accept when selling. The order is added to the order book and only executes if the market reaches the set price. Limit orders may remain unfilled if the market does not move to the specified price.

**Important notes:**

*   Market orders provide fast entry and exit but the filled price is not guaranteed, especially in volatile markets.
    
*   Limit orders give traders more control over price but may not execute if the market never reaches the chosen level.
    

**Stop limit order:** A Stop-Limit order combines a stop price with a limit order. When the stop price is reached, it triggers a limit order to buy or sell at the limit price or better.

Key terms:

*   **Stop price:** The price that triggers the order. Once the asset reaches this price, the limit order becomes active.
    
*   **Limit price:** The minimum price you are willing to sell at, or the maximum price you are willing to buy at. The order will only execute at this price or better.
    
*   **Quantity:** The number of tokens you want to buy or sell.
    

[PreviousSpot Fee Structure](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-spot/spot-fee-structure)
[NextPost Only & TIF](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-spot/post-only-and-tif)

# Hedge Mode | Aster

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/hedge-mode#what-is-hedge-mode)

What is Hedge Mode?

Hedge Mode is a strategic approach used by futures traders to manage and mitigate market risk. This strategy allows traders to open two opposing positions—a long and a short—under the same contract, enabling them to capitalize on market fluctuations while minimizing potential losses.

#### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-perpetual-pro/hedge-mode#difference-between-one-way-mode-and-hedge-mode)

Difference Between One-Way Mode and Hedge Mode

1.  **One-Way Mode**
    
    In One-Way Mode, traders can hold positions in only one direction per contract. If you open a position anticipating a market move in a single direction, you cannot simultaneously open an opposite position without canceling or reducing the existing one.
    
2.  **Hedge Mode**
    
    Hedge Mode allows traders to hold both long and short positions at the same time under the same contract. For instance, you can maintain both long and short positions in a BTCUSDT contract simultaneously. This flexibility helps traders adapt to market dynamics and manage their risk more effectively across different timeframes.
    

**How to switch between One-Way Mode and Hedge Mode?**

1.  Open the trading interface and click the button of settings.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FhfeBDVPFoV3Nhrox9fkS%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-08-18%252016.30.26.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7535b602-c866-4239-98f8-4731f7e12057&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c3d87684&sv=2)

1.  Click the Position Mode and you could switch from One-Way Mode to Hedge Mode.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FxfPhtTDDVq22Y7gZ7TvG%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-08-18%252016.28.17.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd5f66bf6-f7ae-4f13-a8d6-2e58d728dede&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=666c9452&sv=2)

1.  Select between One-Way Mode or Hedge Mode.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FRZl3jMhHcdY4PobquFtS%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-08-18%252016.31.46.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D44e27fc0-6def-46f4-a81c-ef8363132498&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ac83e4b1&sv=2)

_**Please note that Position Mode cannot be adjusted while you have open positions or open orders.**_

# Tutorial/Guide | Aster

If you joined the Four.meme CDL presale, here’s what to expect:

*   Airdrop time: 12:00 UTC/20:00 HK on Septermber 2nd
    
*   Distribution: Eligible users will automatically receive $CDL in their Aster Spot wallet once the window opens
    

**Steps**

1.  Connect your wallet to Aster Spot.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252Fgjr6exP721mcRPSCNDOi%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-09-02%252008.49.25.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddc69edec-c5bc-4544-9e71-e74c6b948d33&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4be73ed8&sv=2)

1.  Sign the verification transaction.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FQSBMyOT7VIMe6acRRCqc%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-09-02%252015.29.39.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9368765d-f930-4a40-a45e-f916decee9f7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5cac2e80&sv=2)

1.  Check your spot account to view your $CDL balance.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FhNjWV7MRaAoY4p5rTxXg%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-09-02%252018.23.34.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1858f41a-56ce-41ec-8f8e-a9c7d62c221b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4dc77c24&sv=2)

1.  To sell your CDL tokens, select the trading pair, enter the quantity, and choose an order type to place your trade.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FkV2p4Hst2o2QDkwKZgtx%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-09-02%252018.36.33.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D492eac43-5f90-4282-be36-e2ea36b7dbfe&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4ef586ca&sv=2)

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FbpewTrAeihBtitD2FXnb%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-09-02%252018.37.52.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbc858139-1dab-43da-b8a8-1a3193cef47b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ae465906&sv=2)

1.  After that, start the withdrawal process in your Aster perpetual account as shown below.
    

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252F4FqPDjPpAWQm48SiGCmM%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-09-02%252018.39.43.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4a1ef7cc-e69c-40b6-9453-342ef92adcb2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=faf5a6eb&sv=2)

**Special Reminder:** If you have multiple accounts, please follow the instructions: https://github.com/asterdex/api-docs/blob/master/consolidation.js

_**Note**__: Your CDL airdrop allocation is not directly proportional to the amount of presale tokens you submitted on Four.meme. Any remaining allocation will be refunded by Four.meme to your wallet. Please check_ [_the Four.meme website_](https://four.meme/)
 _for full details._

# Aster Spot | Aster

Spot trading is a direct transaction between a buyer and a seller at the current market rate, known as the spot price.

For example, in the BTC/USDT pair, you can buy or sell 1 BTC at the spot price and pay or receive the equivalent amount in USDT.

**What’s the difference between spot trading and perpetuals trading?**

In spot trading, traders buy and sell the actual tokens of the underlying assets. For example, buying BTC in the spot market means you hold BTC in your account and benefit if its value increases.

In perpetuals trading, traders do not own the underlying asset. Instead, they trade perpetual contracts based on price movements. Perpetuals allow traders to go long when bullish or go short when bearish, without holding the actual token.

[PreviousInteract with the contract directly](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/interact-with-the-contract-directly)
[NextDeposit & Withdrawal Guide](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-spot/deposit-and-withdrawal-guide)

# Post Only & TIF | Aster

**Post Only**

When placing a limit order, you can select Post Only to ensure it does not execute immediately. Instead, the order will be placed on the order book as a maker order, never matching with existing orders already in the book. Maker orders add liquidity, and when your order executes later, you will pay the maker fee rather than the taker fee.

**Time-in-Force** (TIF) determines how long your order remains active before being executed or canceled. This lets you control the duration of your order when placing it. Aster supports three types of TIF orders:

*   **GTC (Good ‘Til Cancelled):** The order stays active until it is filled or you cancel it.
    
*   **IOC (Immediate or Cancel):** The order attempts to execute immediately (fully or partially). Any unfilled portion is canceled. If no quantity is available at your chosen price, the entire order is canceled. Iceberg orders are not supported.
    
*   **FOK (Fill or Kill):** The order must be filled in full immediately, or it will be canceled. Iceberg orders are not supported.
    

[PreviousOrder types](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-spot/order-types)
[NextSupport Center](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-spot/support-center)

# Degen mode | Aster

The [Degen](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/BTCUSD)
 trading mode offers traders high-leverage perpetual trading. During periods of high volatility, traders can maximize their gains with high leverage and extremely low fees. In low volatility, traders can speculate on minor price movements.

Degen trading mode is currently available for BTC/USD, supporting a maximum leverage of 1001x for both long and short market orders. Traders just need to connect and wallet and input a collateral amount before opening a position. There is 0.01% slippage for BTC/USD.

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/degen-mode#degen-mode-features)

**Degen mode features**

*   **Lower price slippage**
    

In Degen mode, enjoy 0.01% slippage for BTC/USD. For lower leverages, trading pairs have either a fixed or dynamic slippage.

*   **0 opening fees**
    

In Degen mode, trading fees do not apply for opening orders. For classic trading pairs and leverage <500x for BTC/USD, 0.08% trading fees are applicable.

*   **Dynamic closing fee for Degen mode**
    

A dynamic PnL fee will be applied for closing positions. This fee is designed to charge fees based on PnL and protect users from losses. For more information, please check [here](https://apollox-finance.gitbook.io/apollox-finance/welcome/trading-on-v2/degen-trading-mode/dynamic-close-fee-for-degen-mode)
.

*   **Unable to add margin to positions**
    

Unlike lower leverages, traders currently cannot add margin to open positions in Degen mode. Traders are advised to monitor the risks and practice responsibility while trading.

**Liquidation**

Liquidation price distance = Entry price \* (Initial margin \* Liquidation lost rate + Accumulated funding fee) / Initial margin / Leverage

Liquidation price

*   Long: Entry price - Liquidation price distance
    
*   Short: Entry price + Liquidation price distance
    

Definitions

*   _Entry price_ is the price at which the trader opens a position
    
*   _Initial margin_ is the user's initial collateral used as margin
    
*   _Liquidation lost rate_ is the forced liquidation lost rate. The default value is 60%.
    
*   _Leverage_ is the user's selected leverage multiple
    

### 

[](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/degen-mode#how-to-trade-degen)

**How to trade Degen**

Access Degen mode from [1001x](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/BTCUSD)
. Select a leverage of 500x or higher to enter Degen mode.

Connect your wallet, enter your collateral amount, and select a leverage. Click on _Advanced_ to choose a [take profit/stop loss](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/aster-pro/order-types#tp-sl-take-profit-stop-loss)
.

The max net profit ROI will be around 500% for 500x and 750x, and 300% for 1001x.

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FVzDeMceS2V3K5hXUTuvm%252FScreenshot%25202025-08-19%2520at%252018.48.54.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da7ab9fe0-8469-40cd-95a2-7d69632b140e&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b419261b&sv=2)

[PreviousFees & slippage](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/1001x-simple/fees-and-slippage)
